## Section 001: Image Generation Prompt Patterns
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title opens the theme without naming the source's governing split, a default built-in image_gen mode and an explicit-only CLI fallback whose controls must never leak into each other
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the local skill states the CLI may be used only when the user explicitly asks, so any guidance that blurs the mode boundary teaches agents to break the skill's first rule
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the two-mode framing does not apply when the task should not use image generation at all, such as extending an existing SVG icon system or building visuals in HTML/CSS
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the patterns govern prompting and mode selection for raster image generation and do not govern vector asset editing or code-native visuals
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open by stating the two top-level modes and the rule that fallback CLI mode is entered only on explicit user request, never automatically
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the skill treats mode choice as a permission question rather than a capability question, the CLI exists but consent, not convenience, gates it
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to prompt through the shared labeled-spec schema and run the built-in image_gen tool, reserving the scripts/image_gen.py CLI for explicit user requests only
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because the local skill states the CLI may be used only when the user explicitly asks, so any guidance that blurs the mode boundary teaches agents to break the skill's first rule
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; the two-mode framing does not apply when the task should not use image generation at all, such as extending an existing SVG icon system or building visuals in HTML/CSS
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the patterns govern prompting and mode selection for raster image generation and do not govern vector asset editing or code-native visuals
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: open by stating the two top-level modes and the rule that fallback CLI mode is entered only on explicit user request, never automatically
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Image Generation Prompt Patterns", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the skill treats mode choice as a permission question rather than a capability question, the CLI exists but consent, not convenience, gates it

### Question 04: When does it fail or become the wrong choice?

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed registry lists three corpus-hygiene failures and omits the anti-patterns the source itself legislates against, silent CLI fallback, unimplied creative augmentation, forgotten edit invariants, and assets stranded at default save paths
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the SKILL.md writes explicit never-rules for these behaviors because they are the failures that actually ship, wrong-mode runs and drifting edits
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: an exhaustive import of every source rule would duplicate the skill instead of registering the highest-cost patterns
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry names prompting and mode failures with detection signals and does not restate the full workflow

## Section 008: Verification Gate Command Set
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed gate names one repository verifier command while the source's real gates are visual and procedural, output inspection against the spec, text-verbatim checks, and the CLI's --dry-run payload preview
- **supporting_reason:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because an image can pass every text lint and still fail its only meaningful test, looking wrong, so gates must include the inspect-and-validate step the workflow mandates
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: visual gates cannot be scripted into this corpus's verifier, so the section must distinguish automatable from judgment gates
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the gate set defines what must pass before generated assets are trusted and does not implement the review itself
- **revision_decision:** Section 008 "Verification Gate Command Set", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to keep the repository verifier and add the source's checkable gates, --dry-run payload preview for CLI work, verbatim text comparison, and the subject-style-composition inspection pass

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide says use this reference when the theme is mentioned, but the real trigger is an act, an agent is about to generate, edit, or batch raster assets and must first decide mode and intent
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because mode and intent decisions attach at request time, and a guide keyed to topic mentions fires too late or not at all
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: keying to every image mention would open this reference for tasks the skill itself excludes, like extending an SVG icon set
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide routes readers into this reference and does not decide augmentation depth, which the tradeoff guide owns
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to trigger on generate, edit, and batch events, with the skill's decision tree resolving intent and its two-mode rule resolving execution
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the source splits every request into two orthogonal questions, intent and execution strategy, and most misfires come from answering only one of them
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 011: Decision Tradeoff Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide keys adopt, adapt, and avoid to generic evidence agreement instead of the variables the source uses, prompt specificity, intent type, and whether the asset is preview-only or project-bound
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because augmentation depth is the real decision, and the source allocates it by how specific the user already was, not by evidence agreement
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: specificity-keyed advice under-determines edits, where the binding variable is invariant preservation rather than augmentation
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide calibrates prompting effort per request and cannot waive the no-invention rule once a prompt is specific
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rekey adopt to normalizing detailed prompts, adapt to tastefully augmenting generic ones, and avoid to declining generation when vector or code-native output fits better
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the source prices effort by reversibility, preview-only work tolerates loose prompting while project-bound and edit work demand full constraint discipline
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to match augmentation to specificity, match invariant discipline to intent, and match delivery rigor to whether the asset is project-bound
- **supporting_reason:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: prefer that default because augmentation depth is the real decision, and the source allocates it by how specific the user already was, not by evidence agreement
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: do not present the default as universal; specificity-keyed advice under-determines edits, where the binding variable is invariant preservation rather than augmentation
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: the guide calibrates prompting effort per request and cannot waive the no-invention rule once a prompt is specific
- **revision_decision:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: rekey adopt to normalizing detailed prompts, adapt to tastefully augmenting generic ones, and avoid to declining generation when vector or code-native output fits better
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 011 "Decision Tradeoff Guide", Question 02 on recommended default: explain that the default also implies the source prices effort by reversibility, preview-only work tolerates loose prompting while project-bound and edit work demand full constraint discipline
### Question 03: When does the default work well?

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model caps work at ten source files and three delegated subtasks per run, while image workload is really bounded by assets per request, iterations per asset, and batch concurrency
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the costly unit here is a generation call, and a model blind to call counts cannot budget the thing that actually consumes time and spend
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: call-count budgets vary by asset stakes, a brand hero justifies iterations a placeholder never will
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the model bounds generation effort per request and does not bound the creative scope of the assets themselves
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rebound the model around one spec per asset, single-change iterations until acceptance, and batches run through per-asset built-in calls or explicit CLI generate-batch with bounded concurrency
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the source builds backpressure into batch tooling itself, generate-batch defaults to concurrency five and requires an output directory, bounding both parallelism and file sprawl

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bullets classify verification failures generically and never define this theme's retry semantics, what to change when a render misses, when to stop iterating, and how batch retries are bounded
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because an unguided retry loop rewrites the whole prompt each time, destroying the attribution that tells you which change fixed what
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: single-change iteration is slow for exploratory work where the user wants divergent options rather than convergence
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this governs retries of generation attempts, not retries of the network layer, which the fallback CLI's max-attempts flag handles
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add iteration semantics, one targeted change per retry with invariants restated, and batch semantics, bounded concurrency with per-job failure isolation
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the source's retry unit is a delta, not a do-over, each follow-up changes exactly one thing so failure attribution survives the loop

## Section 024: Scale Boundary Statement
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed statement recites multi-system and SLO limits and misses this theme's scale walls, batch jobs beyond ad-hoc prompting, asset libraries needing consistent style across many sessions, and model churn retiring parameter facts
- **supporting_reason:** Section 024 "Scale Boundary Statement", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because prompting patterns scale by templating, and past some asset count the unit of work becomes the JSONL manifest and the shared spec template, not the individual prompt
